  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer5207947506347186131">Eckhart Tolle is rapidly emerging as one of the world’s most inspiring spiritual teachers, sharing the enlightenment he himself experienced after a startling personal transformation. His views go beyond any particular religion, doctrine, or guru. This book extracts the essence from his teachings in The Power of Now, showing us how to free ourselves from “enslavement to the</span>
  <span id="freeText5207947506347186131" style="display:none">Eckhart Tolle is rapidly emerging as one of the world’s most inspiring spiritual teachers, sharing the enlightenment he himself experienced after a startling personal transformation. His views go beyond any particular religion, doctrine, or guru. This book extracts the essence from his teachings in The Power of Now, showing us how to free ourselves from “enslavement to the mind.” The aim is to be able to enter into and sustain an awakened state of consciousness throughout everyday life. Through meditations and simple techniques, Eckhart shows us how to quiet our thoughts, see the world in the present moment, and find a path to “a life of grace, ease, and lightness.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="5207947506347186131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/499165-i-am-still-reading-this-book-and-already">I am still reading this book, and already I feel the transformative power effect. 
Can some body assist with practical guidance, from experience on how, they have manage to put it into practice?

Thanks</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/16025522-jimmy-imd"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1357181599i/16025522._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/16025522-jimmy-imd">Jimmy Imd</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">it has work really well for me. I read this book and felt it's msg and experienced the deep peace of NOW. However the mind was pretty much active and <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">it has work really well for me. I read this book and felt it's msg and experienced the deep peace of NOW. However the mind was pretty much active and had good amount of control over me when I am not consciously practicing. It's only until recently that that the troubles and problems seem to start engulfing me again and triggered me to look within myself for answers. and so I did a speak on the summary of what the mind is about in a public speaking club and joined an discussion group as well. through it, it dawn on me that I was judging everything and everyone the whole time. Or rather, it was my mind which I allowed myself to associate with. With that consciousness within me, I watched myself in almost every waking, catching my mind's activities and just disassociating from the passing thoughts. Through that, my emotional health has improved positively, my relationship with my wife, family members and friends have improved too. I freed myself from the burden of judgment. As a result I am able to accept more and love more. for that I am grateful. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50147177?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Polina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Polina" href="/user/show/1937650-polina">Polina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50147177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15401671763889604624">I never managed to complete reading the Power of Now although tried several times. This book was a god send, and even though it still suffers from what seems to be repetition of the same principle on every page, since it is a lot shorter I have read it in a day and feel like I have fully grasped everything that Eckhart was trying to convey in his main book. So if you, like me, find the Power Of Now a difficult read this book will definitely give you all the main ideas in a concise digestible for</span>
  <span id="freeText15401671763889604624" style="display:none">I never managed to complete reading the Power of Now although tried several times. This book was a god send, and even though it still suffers from what seems to be repetition of the same principle on every page, since it is a lot shorter I have read it in a day and feel like I have fully grasped everything that Eckhart was trying to convey in his main book. So if you, like me, find the Power Of Now a difficult read this book will definitely give you all the main ideas in a concise digestible form. <br />I think this book will make for a perfect every day companion as the author suggests to read one paragraph or section every day to reflect and to remind yourself of the practice. Might also make a good intro to Power Of Now if you want to introduce your friends or relatives to the ideas put forward.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38199655" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16719621461350685803">Tolle has a way of giving meaning to life by using exercises, meditations and essential teachings (many based on Eastern philosophies) to bring peace, balance and harmony into our lives. The goal is to be able to bring about and sustain an enlightened state of consciousness in our immediate existence. <br/><br/><br/>I'm particularly attracted to the Budhist, Hindu, and Taoist notion of "no-self", relinquishing the ego so that life's challenges do not impact you, rather you flow through and around them. In my o</span>
  <span id="freeText16719621461350685803" style="display:none">Tolle has a way of giving meaning to life by using exercises, meditations and essential teachings (many based on Eastern philosophies) to bring peace, balance and harmony into our lives. The goal is to be able to bring about and sustain an enlightened state of consciousness in our immediate existence. <br /><br /><br />I'm particularly attracted to the Budhist, Hindu, and Taoist notion of "no-self", relinquishing the ego so that life's challenges do not impact you, rather you flow through and around them. In my opinion, this philosophy embodies what self-confidence wants to be when it grows up.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203497414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12965071665882195510">This book contains many strategies to help us lead a richer, more satisfying life. In many ways it's the work journal or exercise of Tolle's previous work, however it contains many quotable lines which you want to come back to. Here are a couple:<br/><br/>"To be identified with your mind is to be trapped in time: the compulsion to live almost exclusively through memory and anticipation...the past gives you an identity and the future holds the promise of salvation, of fulfillment...Both are illusions." (p.</span>
  <span id="freeText12965071665882195510" style="display:none">This book contains many strategies to help us lead a richer, more satisfying life. In many ways it's the work journal or exercise of Tolle's previous work, however it contains many quotable lines which you want to come back to. Here are a couple:<br /><br />"To be identified with your mind is to be trapped in time: the compulsion to live almost exclusively through memory and anticipation...the past gives you an identity and the future holds the promise of salvation, of fulfillment...Both are illusions." (p.31)<br /><br />"Wherever you are, be there totally. Stress is caused by being 'here' but wanting to be 'there'. It's the split that tears you apart inside." (p.50)<br /><br />I read this book in one sitting, however because of its mantra-like repetition of key concepts, I think it would be better to dip into it from time to time, reminding oneself of the need to take time out to achieve balance, to centre our beings in tranquillity, to take fully immerse our self in the moment rather than looking forward or back.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10502045122873272308">Practicing the Power of Now is a handy companion to Eckhart’s wildly popular The Power of Now. Essentially, Practicing the Power of Now contains the same information as in the first book. However, I have to say that I prefer this format. The first book was written in a question answer format. These questions came from the author’s students. He also included amalgamated questions that covered a variety of common queries. These question and answer sessions gradually took the reader from common per</span>
  <span id="freeText10502045122873272308" style="display:none">Practicing the Power of Now is a handy companion to Eckhart’s wildly popular The Power of Now. Essentially, Practicing the Power of Now contains the same information as in the first book. However, I have to say that I prefer this format. The first book was written in a question answer format. These questions came from the author’s students. He also included amalgamated questions that covered a variety of common queries. These question and answer sessions gradually took the reader from common perception through to an understanding of the illusions that we generally accept as real and the importance of the present moment. <br /><br />Practicing the Power of Now is written in formalized chapters summarizing much of the material written that first book such as being and enlightenment; the origin of fear, entering the now, dissolving consciousness, etc. The best quotations, mediations, and exercises first previously presented are also included. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10502045122873272308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_381556633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381556633" />
    <a title="S&#39;hi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/784353-s-hi"><img alt="S&#39;hi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381556633?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S&#39;hi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S&#39;hi" href="/user/show/784353-s-hi">S&#39;hi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381556633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer736500965139600396">Although this is the companion workbook to The Power of Now, which was published in 1997, my familiarity with the material and many of the processes have enabled me to read through it all in a couple of hours. From this point of view I can agree with Tolle’s suggestion in the introduction that it is an Introduction to the grander version in his previous book. However, it is still quite a substantial volume for a beginning of awareness for anyone who has not had any prior experience of this kind </span>
  <span id="freeText736500965139600396" style="display:none">Although this is the companion workbook to The Power of Now, which was published in 1997, my familiarity with the material and many of the processes have enabled me to read through it all in a couple of hours. From this point of view I can agree with Tolle’s suggestion in the introduction that it is an Introduction to the grander version in his previous book. However, it is still quite a substantial volume for a beginning of awareness for anyone who has not had any prior experience of this kind of work.<br /><br />My suggestion would be that a newcomer to the idea of meditation or mind awareness would benefit from reading through the volume reasonably quickly, perhaps jotting a few notes of the pages which seem most difficult to connect with. Then a second reading allowing plenty of time to practice the exercises will allow the more familiar and the less familiar to balance each other rather than feeling like too daunting a task.<br /><br />Once some familiarity has been achieved, Tolle’s own suggestion of randomly opening the book to read or practice an exercise will already have some foundation upon which to anchor its practice more readily. There are also a few quotes of one or two lines well worth writing out to display for triggering attention as you go about your daily tasks.<br /><br />A handy little volume to refer to on a regular basis.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="736500965139600396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17701543126781363259">i don't know what to think, man. it's not that the basis of this isn't sound.   <span id="freeText17701543126781363259" style="display:none">i don't know what to think, man. it's not that the basis of this isn't sound. Suffering comes from resistance; wishing that circumstances were other than they were, insisting that something 'shouldn't' be happening. Suffering comes from living in the past, or the future. But there are other books - a fuckton of other books - that can guide you through this. Tolle wouldn't be the first writer I'd suggest to someone interested in dealing with life challenges in a way that brings you peace.<br /><br />Because that whole binary gender only completed by "opposite energy polarity" thing? Yeah, nah. Fuck that. <br /><br />On the other hand, I've been meaning to read this for <i>twenty years</i>, and I feel a great deal of satisfaction knowing I finally did (whether or not it was worth the wait.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17701543126781363259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16626789593670587930" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book. I vowed to stay away from self help books, but I could not resist borrowing this slim book from a coworker. I feel like it can really change my mind-if I let it. <br /><br />The sections that dealt with controlling your mind stood out especially since my mind kept wandering all over the place while trying to read this book. It made me realize just how difficult it is for me to focus. I have been practicing reeling my mind in since reading this book.<br /><br />The portions on the Ego also made a ton of sense. I agree that the ego likes drama and chaos. I also agree that there are some people who love living in the past because those memories make them who they are. More attention should be focused on Now. <br /><br />The end lost me a bit and I struggled to stay focus and comeplete the book, but overall it is a good read.</span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182234221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13839202917847264756">A friend of mine is completely smitten with Tolle's book The Power of Now, and insisted that I read this smaller book while I was visiting him over the long weekend. Although I found a few things that resonated with me, most of that was of the "stop and smell the roses" type philosophy that I've believed for a long time. Most of the rest of it I found ridiculous - especially that people who act badly are under the influence of their "pain bodies" and therefore not responsible for their actions. </span>
  <span id="freeText13839202917847264756" style="display:none">A friend of mine is completely smitten with Tolle's book The Power of Now, and insisted that I read this smaller book while I was visiting him over the long weekend. Although I found a few things that resonated with me, most of that was of the "stop and smell the roses" type philosophy that I've believed for a long time. Most of the rest of it I found ridiculous - especially that people who act badly are under the influence of their "pain bodies" and therefore not responsible for their actions. I'm sure there was a lot in there that I missed, but I was so turned off by the terminology that I just couldn't take it seriously.</span>

<div id="review_1894606714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894606714" />
    <a title="Jim Dennison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16126383-jim-dennison"><img alt="Jim Dennison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399833986p2/16126383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894606714?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Dennison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Dennison" href="/user/show/16126383-jim-dennison">Jim Dennison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894606714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2202585819136649338">I've been aware of Tolle for a few years - but had never really had the time or motivation to read his somewhat hefty books on the 'Power of Now'.<br/><br/>This condensed edition is much more accessible. Important because I'd say that to get maximum benefit you really need to read its content many times - to internalise it and 'brainwash' yourself.<br/><br/>It's message is to me fascinating. It's general ideas resonate with Eastern philosophies (and actually the Mexican Yacqui shaman ideas) but it is not couched in</span>
  <span id="freeText2202585819136649338" style="display:none">I've been aware of Tolle for a few years - but had never really had the time or motivation to read his somewhat hefty books on the 'Power of Now'.<br /><br />This condensed edition is much more accessible. Important because I'd say that to get maximum benefit you really need to read its content many times - to internalise it and 'brainwash' yourself.<br /><br />It's message is to me fascinating. It's general ideas resonate with Eastern philosophies (and actually the Mexican Yacqui shaman ideas) but it is not couched in mysterious or religious terms. It's much more straightforward.<br /><br />My interpretation is that the book highlights a negative side effect of human brain evolution (or as Tolle puts it '3000 years of social conditioning'). <br /><br />Which is our assumption - perhaps addiction - that our identity, who we are, is that voice in our head. Our attention. Our Ego. And everything else is 'separate', even our own bodies.<br /><br />While for most of us, most of the time this can be a source of familiarity, comfort and an ability to plan, learn, and 'succeed', it is also the SAME source of pain, anxiety, depression - The Human Condition - even suicide.<br /><br />Tolle teaches that we CAN move out of this unconscious state of 'being our thoughts' and achieve a purer state of being TRULY alive and all that comes with it.<br /><br />Unlike the Ego which lives exclusively in the past, future, or alternative realities (daydreaming) we should live purely in The Now. <br /><br />Tolle suggests we achieve this by treating our Ego - our inner voice - as an Object like any other. It is not us. It's just an object with no meaning. In fact it's like a needy selfish child and we should acknowledge its presence but ignore it's wheedling and it's judgements. <br /><br />Instead the real us - 'The Watcher' - should focus on observing and experiencing without judgement. <br /><br />Watching and experiencing our bodies and their subtle physical sensations (emotions, and a low thrum of aliveness which most of us fail to even notice). <br /><br />Watching and experiencing the world. Watching and experiencing our actions. Being conscious of such things but not 'thinking about' or judging them.<br /><br />Tolle acknowledges that this is hard work - getting the best things in life usually are - because we live in our comfort zone fearing change. Even if that zone includes feelings of fear, anxiety and self - judgement.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2202585819136649338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_114111345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114111345" />
    <a title="Lynne Tull" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3972804-lynne-tull"><img alt="Lynne Tull" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585254414p2/3972804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114111345?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynne Tull" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynne Tull" href="/user/show/3972804-lynne-tull">Lynne Tull</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3972804-lynne-tull?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114111345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer838364852105735118">Every once in a while information comes to me just when I need it. Sometimes it is a single word from a stranger, sometimes, a friend. This time is was in the form of a book: The Power of Now . I have to admit that I didn’t understand many of the concepts presented. I have gotten from it what I need for “Now”.<br/> <br/>Two things stand out as I think about what I want to tell you about me and The Power of Now.<br/><br/>One: When I say “I am so mad at myself”, who is the “I” and who is the “myself”? Mr. Tolle ident</span>
  <span id="freeText838364852105735118" style="display:none">Every once in a while information comes to me just when I need it. Sometimes it is a single word from a stranger, sometimes, a friend. This time is was in the form of a book: The Power of Now . I have to admit that I didn’t understand many of the concepts presented. I have gotten from it what I need for “Now”.<br /> <br />Two things stand out as I think about what I want to tell you about me and The Power of Now.<br /><br />One: When I say “I am so mad at myself”, who is the “I” and who is the “myself”? Mr. Tolle identifies the “I” as the conscious or the inner self. The unconscious is the face I present to people as I act out my life situation. As I act out my life situation, I will find peace if I stay as long as I can in the Now. I do not dwell on the past or the future it is a part of my life situation. The goal is to strive to deal with the life situation from the conscious inner self, my real self, as an impartial observer/participant. <br /><br />Eckhart Tolle: “Nothing exists outside the Now. Nothing ever happened in the past; it happened in the Now. Nothing will ever happen in the future: it will happen in the Now.” <br /><br />Two: When I experience a “life situation” that is not pleasant and even painful, I have three choices:<br />1) stop doing what I am doing 2) if a person is involved, I need to speak to the person concerned and express fully what I feel or 3) drop the negativity that my mind has created around the situation and serves no purpose.<br /><br />I can recommend this book and its concepts to you. I also would suggest that you read it through the first time. Then, you can go back to particular parts that may speak to you at that moment in the Now.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="838364852105735118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="R" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25961995-r"><img alt="R" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1464287821?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R" href="/user/show/25961995-r">R</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25961995-r?shelf=philosophy-and-spirituality">philosophy-and-spirituality</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1464287821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17912079433272954906">Before starting this book, I thought it was a follow up on The Power Of Now. However, it is not so. The author himself writes that this book is the gist of The Power Of Now; in case someone finds it too daunting to read, they could read this one. <br/><br/>My reason for 3 stars is not the content of the book, it is more for a misleading title. Even though it lists a few exercises on how to remain in the present moment, those exercises are few and far in between and most of the book is just a repetition of</span>
  <span id="freeText17912079433272954906" style="display:none">Before starting this book, I thought it was a follow up on The Power Of Now. However, it is not so. The author himself writes that this book is the gist of The Power Of Now; in case someone finds it too daunting to read, they could read this one. <br /><br />My reason for 3 stars is not the content of the book, it is more for a misleading title. Even though it lists a few exercises on how to remain in the present moment, those exercises are few and far in between and most of the book is just a repetition of The Power Of Now. <br /><br />If I had read this before The Power Of Now, I would surely have skipped reading it. I am glad I did not. The Power Of Now is one of the most amazing books I've read on the workings of the human mind. If you have read that, you can surely give this book a miss. But if you are deciding on not reading that based on this one, do reconsider it. This book doesn't seem to convey the ideas of the authors in the same depth as The Power Of Now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17912079433272954906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16433993564232369024" style="display:none">I'm not sure why I didn't like this book as much as the other Eckhart Tolle books I've read.<br />It might be because I read it in Danish and so felt a bit disconnected to his voice and the flow just wasn't the same, or it could also be that this book just wasn't as good of course.<br /><br />Either way, this book summed up some of the main thoughts and served as a good little reminder. It was an enjoyable read, making me more aware and focused on some issues to work on or connect with more in my daily humdrum life.<br /><br />I still feel the power of Tolles words brings me one step closer to the power of Now.</span>

<div id="review_194161010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194161010" />
    <a title="Dustin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5955541-dustin"><img alt="Dustin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389485902p2/5955541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194161010?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dustin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dustin" href="/user/show/5955541-dustin">Dustin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194161010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1545703768985819308">This is a great book that compliments a Power of Now. If you're interested in growing spiritually and finding more happiness, I highly recommend anything by Eckhart Tolle. Much of his teachings are not new--the main ideas have been presented by countless of people through much of history. However, the way he presents it is fresh and easy to understand for people living a Western lifestyle. I highly recommend reading a New Earth first. Start on chapter 3.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GJF/CP0YpZI7qpdxHPMiDmDUAQbjx5QtlDEt5sniDxEB3/Q0TAQULRe0LYc2AgmB/mTfDsKu5wcLhBcbJD5Kyw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZE3Z0CDn+EvGnNYmUk8fdOZmrtwcoWrlAnQelKsUCeF9A1LskftJ9OqCbNB4vjT7eNZw1D3IGc+dwSRpRshMOw==')})
  }

The Seat of the Soul became a national bestseller when it was first published, but more people are buying it now than ever before. Why is this?  It is because a new species is being born. The Seat of the Soul is about this birth. This new species longs for harmony, cooperation, sharing, and reverence for Life. It uses higher orders of logic and justice -- those of the heart. The number of people who are becoming aware of this birth is growing very fast, because the new species is being born inside all of us.  The Seat of the Soul provides a vocabulary for this new species -- a vocabulary of authentic power, the alignment of the personality with the soul. Human experience is exploding beyond the five senses, and The Seat of the Soul is about that, too. This is the most exciting time to be on Earth, and The Seat of the Soul describes why. I have been writing a book about this new potential for nine years. I am looking forward to sharing that with you, too.  The tremendous growth of interest in The Seat of the Soul is humbling to me. I dream of a world where people respect each other and the living Earth, and spiritual growth is the first priority. I work daily to develop the awareness, compassion, and intentions that are necessary to create it. The extraordinary reception of The Seat of the Soul shows me, among other things, how many fellow souls are doing the same. The classic text of these 81 verses, called the Tao Te Ching or the Great Way, offers advice and guidance that is balanced, moral, spiritual, and always concerned with working for the good.\n\nIn this book, Dr. Wayne W. Dyer has reviewed hundreds of translations of the Tao Te Ching and has written 81 distinct essays on how to apply the ancient wisdom of Lao-tzu to today’s modern world. This work contains the entire 81 verses of the Tao, compiled from Wayne’s researching of 12 of the most well-respected translations of text that have survived for more than 25 centuries. Each chapter is designed for actually living the Tao or the Great Way today. Some of the chapter titles are “Living with Flexibility,” “Living Without Enemies,” and “Living by Letting Go.” Each of the 81 brief chapters focuses on living the Tao and concludes with a section called “Doing the Tao Now.”\n\n        Wayne spent one entire year reading, researching, and meditating on Lao-tzu’s messages, practicing them each day and ultimately writing down these essays as he felt Lao-tzu wanted you to know them.\n\nThis is a work to be read slowly, one essay a day. As Wayne says, “This is a book that will forever change the way you look at your life, and the result will be that you’ll live in a new world aligned with nature. Writing this book changed me forever, too. I now live in accord with the natural world and feel the greatest sense of peace I’ve ever experienced.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4493.Eckhart_Tolle">About Eckhart Tolle</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12133221874624900907">Eckhart Tolle , born Ulrich Leonard Tolle, February 16, 1948, is a German-born writer, public speaker, and spiritual teacher. The New York Times has called him "the most popular spiritual author in the nation". He is the author of the bestsellers "The Power of Now" and "A New Earth".<br/>Tolle had an unhappy childhood in Germany and Spain. His depression reached its peak during early adulthood in Engla</span>
  <span id="freeText12133221874624900907" style="display:none">Eckhart Tolle , born Ulrich Leonard Tolle, February 16, 1948, is a German-born writer, public speaker, and spiritual teacher. The New York Times has called him "the most popular spiritual author in the nation". He is the author of the bestsellers "The Power of Now" and "A New Earth".<br />Tolle had an unhappy childhood in Germany and Spain. His depression reached its peak during early adulthood in England, until he underwent what he calls an "inner transformation". He then spent many years as a vagrant, "in a a state of deep bliss", he says, before becoming a spiritual teacher. He eventually moved to North America where he began writing his first book. He currently lives in Vancouver, Canada with his wife, Kim Eng.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12133221874624900907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
